<span id="freeTextContainer13866331758315053840"><b>
  <u>SPOILERS AHOY!</u>
</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>4 STARS<br/><blockquote>”You are better than I expected.”<br/>“I am always better than people expect,” Han said.</blockquote></b>
</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394936983ra/8926572.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Oh come on, don’t tell me you didn’t think a little bit of that guy.<br/><br/>I loved this book by the way! Love love love love love.<br/><br/><b>LOVE.</b><br/><br/><b>THERE’S NOTHING COHERENT IN THIS REVIEW. NOTHING.</b><br/><br/>I’m just going to madly flap here and there, over the overwhelming levels of squee, like a fish out of water. <br/><br/>One thing I noticed and liked about this is how each of the characters have grown in a pace that does</span>
  <span id="freeText13866331758315053840" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>SPOILERS AHOY!</u>
</b><br><br><i>
  <b>4 STARS<br><blockquote>”You are better than I expected.”<br>“I am always better than people expect,” Han said.</blockquote></b>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394936983ra/8926572.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh come on, don’t tell me you didn’t think a little bit of that guy.<br><br>I loved this book by the way! Love love love love love.<br><br><b>LOVE.</b><br><br><b>THERE’S NOTHING COHERENT IN THIS REVIEW. NOTHING.</b><br><br>I’m just going to madly flap here and there, over the overwhelming levels of squee, like a fish out of water. <br><br>One thing I noticed and liked about this is how each of the characters have grown in a pace that doesn’t screw with logic. Especially Raisa. I like the way how Raisa still second guesses herself, how she can still be petty and cruel in her seventeen-year old mind. It has only been a year since the events covered in <i>The Demon King</i> after all. This was a great study on how to develop characters believably and how to make the reader fall in love with them slowly. It is that kind of falling after all that makes these characters last in our hearts beyond the final pages and the limits of our imagination. <br><br>I am loving the new, yet underplayed dynamic between Amon and Han. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>”Byrne we need to do a better job of protecting the queen,” he said. “Before we know it, she’ll be showing off old battle scars to her ladies whenever she’s in her cups. It won’t help out reputations any.”<br>Amon nodded without smiling. “I agree. We need to do a better job, and we will.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394937031ra/8926578.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The deadpan is so strong on that boy. These two should have a novella together while knitting sweaters, talking about random, domestic things while not talking about random, domestic things. And cats.<br><br>Anxiety behind the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <br>I’m mad nervous about Amon’s future in this series. I’m eyeing Fiona Bayar and Elena Demonai warily. What does Fiona know about that amulet that she wanted to tell Han about before?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> There's a political clusterfuck looming in the horizon, forcing everyone into a deliciously precarious situation. YAY! It’s such an intricate, layered web Chima managed to weave thus far. It’s insane how everyone here pretty much has personal plans, selfish stocks and hidden motives that drive me mad with speculation on what’s going to happen in the final book. <br><br>I enjoyed picking Han’s streetlord brain, how he applies his methods in protecting Raisa, furthering his plans and how I hope he ties both goals together. I’m a bit cheesed off by his current fashion choices and the whole Alger Waterlow business is too horcruxy, Tom Riddle-y for my tastes. But putting all that in perspective with the path both he and Raisa seem to be on, it stops to niggle and piles on the intrigue. Would lessons be learned? Would history repeat itself? What price will both pay?<br><br>Oh fine, I’m going to stop this pretend review and just squee relentlessly on all that Han-Raisa dialogue that was just…<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>”There’s something about a roof, isn’t there?” Han said. “It makes you feel like it doesn’t matter what’s going on below. All of those things that get in the way of your dreams - you’re above them. Anything is possible.”<br>“Anything is possible,” Raisa repeated.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389315300ra/8019247.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As I've said... squeeing. Fish out of water style.<br><br><a href="http://ashwednesday.booklikes.com/post/825724/squeeing-like-a-fish-" rel="nofollow noopener">Also on BookLikes.</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13866331758315053840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2379108334?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423121381" href="/book/show/12973281-the-gray-wolf-throne">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=read-keep">read-keep</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2379108334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7450909555919777119">The cliffhanger is resolved (for the most part) in the first chapter and by the second we get the answers to the last book's biggest mystery, who is the mysterious Crow? (I was completely right!) I wished we'd gotten these answers in the end of the last book! <br/><br/>This book took me forever! It might be the third book but it had a big case of second book syndrome. After an eventful beginning not much happened to advance the story. This really should've been a trilogy. <br/><br/>Raisa's back to being a cranky pr</span>
  <span id="freeText7450909555919777119" style="display:none">The cliffhanger is resolved (for the most part) in the first chapter and by the second we get the answers to the last book's biggest mystery, who is the mysterious Crow? (I was completely right!) I wished we'd gotten these answers in the end of the last book! <br /><br />This book took me forever! It might be the third book but it had a big case of second book syndrome. After an eventful beginning not much happened to advance the story. This really should've been a trilogy. <br /><br />Raisa's back to being a cranky princess again. She even says she knows she's being unreasonable! Even when she means well she comes off abrasive. We keep being told how good she is with words but she's really not good with people. <br /><br />Both our heroes have been keeping secrets and it's finally time for them to come clean. (Mostly ) Usually I like revelations but I had a feeling these were going to go badly. Han's rather unreasonable about the whole she lied to him thing. Maybe they're a good couple after all. <br /><br />Chima's world building isn't the most inventive but I love her words for wizards and amulets. Usually I hate slang and Han has moments where his street slang is too strong but overall it really adds to the world. Another nice touch is that when a charmcaster/jinxfinger heals they take on their patients symptoms. <br /><br />Amon gets a point of view again! (Just one chapter.) I'm so glad he's back friends with Raisa and that she realized how unfair she was to him. Not much Dancer this time but more Cat. And there's even a little of Raisa's solider friends. I wish we'd seen when they found out she's a princess! <br /><br /><br />Who died? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Edon Bryne, Mac Gillan, Queen Marianna, Geoff Montaigne, Trey Archer <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_458989864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/458989864" />
    <a title="Lainey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1047767-lainey"><img alt="Lainey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341070724p2/1047767.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/458989864?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lainey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lainey" href="/user/show/1047767-lainey">Lainey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer458989864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6036598315538165834">I was just so ready for this to be the book that rises above the average quality (for me) of the first two because things are finally moving forward and Raisa is actively fighting to claim her throne...but I just can't...things still bother me about this series. <br/><br/>My biggest gripe is why the lack of fully realized female characters??? Just because Raisa is one of the two protagonists in this book doesn't mean it is alright to basically dismiss the other girls in the novel as trivial, frilly, silly</span>
  <span id="freeText6036598315538165834" style="display:none">I was just so ready for this to be the book that rises above the average quality (for me) of the first two because things are finally moving forward and Raisa is actively fighting to claim her throne...but I just can't...things still bother me about this series. <br /><br />My biggest gripe is why the lack of fully realized female characters??? Just because Raisa is one of the two protagonists in this book doesn't mean it is alright to basically dismiss the other girls in the novel as trivial, frilly, silly, etc. <br /><br />Let us run down the list of female characters of Raisa's age and how they are portrayed: <br />(1) Mellony - "frilly and lightweight" as per Amon's assessment. We're supposed to think she's silly for falling for Micah when we know Micah is only after the throne and is really in love with Raisa. <br /><br />(2) Cat Tyburn - so close to a great female character but is demoted to Raisa's maid and basically gets ordered around by Han. <br /><br />(3) Fiona Bayar - smart and ambitious and is probably up to something nefarious (we don't know yet) but still powerless and flirts with Han a lot when we know he's also in love with Raisa. <br /><br />(4) Night Bird - capable warrior but still in love with Nightwalker who is also in love with Raisa (sensing a pattern here?). <br /><br />(5) Annamaya Dubai - she doesn't even get a single line and is now doomed to marry Amon WHO IS ALSO IN LOVE WITH RAISA (just stop it already!).<br /><br />(6) Melissa Hakkam - she counts even though she's basically only in the story so she can be portrayed as being flirty and silly and so not "what a strong woman should be".<br /><br />(7) Talia - yes, she's here and she's still great but her only substantial scene is when she gets severely injured defending Raisa.<br /><br />This whole issue really gets to me because while this series portrays a great friendship between Dancer and Han, why can't the author do the same for female friendships? Why can't we have a female character who Raisa treats and respects as her equal (not socially of course because she's the queen but you know, personally)? Instead we get other girls who either work for her or who she sees as silly butterflies and therefore not worth her time. Just really, how hard is it to write about supportive loving female friendships? <br /><br />And oh yes, there was a scene where Raisa complains that there aren't more women in her council. That was totally great at first but then nothing comes from it. Maybe it gets addressed in the next book but I'm beginning to think that line was thrown there "to cover the bases" without any intention of following through on it.<br /><br />And another thing, why must strong women always be portrayed as warrior women who can fight with swords and arrows? Why is embroidery or art seen as trivial pursuits suitable only for those with nothing better to do with their lives? Someone's character should not be judged on whether they like shoes and silks as opposed to swords and daggers. Liking pretty things like gowns does not mean someone is shallow and trivial, it just signifies an appreciation of beauty.<br /><br />I probably need to stop reading books about princesses for a while.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6036598315538165834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer586815330073382700">Another excellent installment in this impressively rich young adult fantasy series. <br/><br/>Listening to this series on audiobook this summer with my kids (10 and 13) has been a great experience. The story is so detailed and rich, providing entertainment for all three of us. I'm quite invested at this point and looking forward to the final book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8069828.The_Crimson_Crown__Seven_Realms___4_' title='The Crimson Crown (Seven Realms, #4) by Cinda Williams Chima' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Crimson Crown</a>. Raisa is a strong and likeable heroine, and the former scoundrel Han continues to mature into an equally endearing male lead.<br/><br/>My daughter's fa</span>
  <span id="freeText586815330073382700" style="display:none">Another excellent installment in this impressively rich young adult fantasy series. <br /><br />Listening to this series on audiobook this summer with my kids (10 and 13) has been a great experience. The story is so detailed and rich, providing entertainment for all three of us. I'm quite invested at this point and looking forward to the final book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8069828.The_Crimson_Crown__Seven_Realms___4_" title="The Crimson Crown (Seven Realms, #4) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crimson Crown</a>. Raisa is a strong and likeable heroine, and the former scoundrel Han continues to mature into an equally endearing male lead.<br /><br />My daughter's favourite is Amon, the honourable friend and guard, and she continues to hope for an ending that will satisfy her: "I know they have other stuff to worry about, but maybe they will all end up together in a polyamorous marriage."<br /><br />Can I just say how much I love that?</span>

<div id="review_1564030851" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1564030851" />
    <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books"><img alt="Em Lost In Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522743986p2/11166121.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1564030851?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Em Lost In Books" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books">Em Lost In Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=2010-19">2010-19</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1564030851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15395457028825244013">Third book in Seven Realm series and what a book it was! This book was everything what I want from a penultimate book in a series. It was intense, full of shocks and surprises, faith, sacrifice, trust and treachery. <br/><br/>So many small stories that author has started in previous books intertwined here and were given an astounding conclusions. But the worst thing is those conclusions are now part of a bigger and more intense plot. My imagination is running wild right now thinking about how all this is </span>
  <span id="freeText15395457028825244013" style="display:none">Third book in Seven Realm series and what a book it was! This book was everything what I want from a penultimate book in a series. It was intense, full of shocks and surprises, faith, sacrifice, trust and treachery. <br /><br />So many small stories that author has started in previous books intertwined here and were given an astounding conclusions. But the worst thing is those conclusions are now part of a bigger and more intense plot. My imagination is running wild right now thinking about how all this is going to end. How Clans and Wizard’s Council will react to the dangerous magic which Han is capable of or how Han will be able to rein himself from turning in to evil? I just want to know answers to these. Then of course there are Micah, Amon and Dancer, our secondary characters but each is able to turn the tables.<br /><br />But this book simply belongs to Raisa. It was hard for me to believe her transition from a heart broken, frail teenage to a Queen who made people to obey her with her cleverness, confidence and strong will. She still is heartbroken but never let it affect her decisions she made to keep her kingdom safe from enemies out on the border and within her own council. She knew everyone who seems a friend could be enemy and she had to be very careful. And she was mighty impressive when it was time to rule the kingdom.<br /><br />Author has created such a magical world in this series that I had a difficult time coming out of this world and it was sad. I don’t know how I will survive final book. <br /><br />Enjoyed every minute of reading this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15395457028825244013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EwwwK4DI8cGQ2EJJmCJDvhsoyHegssuKJ9NFOQGBv0+7/hIWXD3KpHi3mjQ+SFjcG1BGBRT1UYTF+/vcPzyhGw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Lyn73FyGh2bbdMYFhIvDFD5ZrcvOP/7pLXc8X2zRei6H29nhgHO8AzMbHngi4dh2PiEjuXp4ZOfPX4K6Umxkeg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/125308.Cinda_Williams_Chima">About Cinda Williams Chima</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/125308.Cinda_Williams_Chima"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1291420167p3/125308.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<a href="/author/show/125308.Cinda_Williams_Chima">Cinda Williams Chima

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11533434974932592037">New York Times bestselling author Cinda Williams Chima comes from a long line of fortune-tellers, musicians and spinners of tales. She began writing romance novels in middle school, which were often confiscated by her teachers.<br/><br/>Her Heir Chronicles series (magic comes to contemporary Ohio) comprises <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/213647.The_Warrior_Heir' title='The Warrior Heir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Warrior Heir</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/500743.The_Wizard_Heir' title='The Wizard Heir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wizard Heir</a> . <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2866413.The_Dragon_Heir' title='The Dragon Heir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dragon Heir</a> The Enchanter Heir, and the Sorcerer Heir. <br/><br/>Chima's</span>
  <span id="freeText11533434974932592037" style="display:none">New York Times bestselling author Cinda Williams Chima comes from a long line of fortune-tellers, musicians and spinners of tales. She began writing romance novels in middle school, which were often confiscated by her teachers.<br /><br />Her Heir Chronicles series (magic comes to contemporary Ohio) comprises <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/213647.The_Warrior_Heir" title="The Warrior Heir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior Heir</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/500743.The_Wizard_Heir" title="The Wizard Heir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wizard Heir</a> . <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2866413.The_Dragon_Heir" title="The Dragon Heir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragon Heir</a> The Enchanter Heir, and the Sorcerer Heir. <br /><br />Chima's Seven Realms series launched with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King" title="The Demon King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demon King</a> in 2009; I<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7801229.The_Exiled_Queen" title="The Exiled Queen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Exiled Queen</a> in 2010. The Gray Wolf Throne in 2011, and The Crimson Crown (2012.).<br /><br />Her Shattered Realms quartet comprises Flamecaster ( 2016) Shadowcaster (2017) Stormcaster (2018) and Deathcaster scheduled for March 5, 2019. <br /><br />Chima is a graduate of Case Western Reserve University and the University of Akron. Chima has been a workshop leader, panelist, and speaker at writing conferences, including the Northern Ohio SCBWI Conference, the Western Reserve Writers’ Conference, and the World Fantasy Convention. She frequently speaks to young writers and readers at schools and libraries nationwide. <br /><br />Chima lives in Ohio with her family, and is always working on her next novel. </span>
